<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="465" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg/200px-Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg/300px-Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg/400px-Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paris_psaulter_gr139_fol5v.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>David glorified by the women of Israel</i> from the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Psalter" title="Paris Psalter">Paris Psalter</a>, example of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_art_(Byzantine)" title="Macedonian art (Byzantine)">Macedonian art (Byzantine)</a> (sometimes called the <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Renaissance" title="Macedonian Renaissance">Macedonian Renaissance</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>The official Bible of the Eastern Orthodox Church contains the <a href="/wiki/Septuagint" title="Septuagint">Septuagint</a> text of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Daniel" title="Book of Daniel">Book of Daniel</a> given in the translation by <a href="/wiki/Theodotion" title="Theodotion">Theodotion</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarchal_Text" title="Patriarchal Text">Patriarchal Text</a> is used for the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[196]</a></sup> Orthodox Christians hold that the Bible is a verbal icon of Christ, as proclaimed by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Nicaea" title="Second Council of Nicaea">7th ecumenical council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1991209_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1991209-204">[197]</a></sup> They refer to the Bible as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_scripture" title="Holy scripture">holy scripture</a>, meaning writings containing the foundational truths of the Christian faith as revealed by Christ and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">Holy Spirit</a> to its divinely inspired human authors. Holy scripture forms the primary and authoritative written witness of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_tradition" title="Holy tradition">holy tradition</a> and is essential as the basis for all Orthodox teaching and belief.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1991209_(quoting_[[John_Chrysostom]]):_"It_is_impossible_for_a_man_to_be_saved_if_he_does_not_read_the_Scriptures."_205-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1991209_(quoting_[[John_Chrysostom]]):_"It_is_impossible_for_a_man_to_be_saved_if_he_does_not_read_the_Scriptures."-205'>[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>Once established as holy scripture, there has never been any question that the Eastern Orthodox Church holds the full list of books to be venerable and beneficial for reading and study,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[199]</a></sup> even though it informally holds some books in higher esteem than others, the four gospels highest of all. Of the subgroups significant enough to be named, the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anagignoskomena" title="Anagignoskomena">Anagignoskomena</a>" (ἀναγιγνωσκόμενα, "things that are read") comprises ten of the Old Testament books rejected in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_canon" title="Protestant canon">Protestant canon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[200]</a></sup> but deemed by the Eastern Orthodox worthy to be read in worship services, even though they carry a lesser esteem than the 39 books of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew canon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[201]</a></sup> The lowest tier contains the remaining books not accepted by either Protestants or Catholics, among them, <a href="/wiki/Psalm_151" title="Psalm 151">Psalm 151</a>. Though it is a psalm, and is in the book of psalms, it is not classified as being within the Psalter (the first 150 psalms).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a very strict sense, it is not entirely orthodox to call the holy scripture the "Word of God". That is a title the Eastern Orthodox Church reserves for Christ, as supported in the scriptures themselves, most explicitly in the first chapter of the gospel of John. God's Word is not hollow, like human words. "God said, 'let there be light'; and there was light."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[203]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Eastern Orthodox Church does not subscribe to the Protestant doctrine of <i><a href="/wiki/Sola_scriptura" title="Sola scriptura">sola scriptura</a></i>. The church has defined what Scripture is; it also interprets what its meaning is.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[204]</a></sup> Christ promised: "When He, the Spirit of truth, has come, He will guide you into all truth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[205]</a></sup>
</p><p>Scriptures are understood to contain historical fact, poetry, idiom, metaphor, simile, moral fable, parable, prophecy and <a href="/wiki/Wisdom_literature" title="Wisdom literature">wisdom literature</a>, and each bears its own consideration in its interpretation. While divinely inspired, the text still consists of words in human languages, arranged in humanly recognisable forms. The Eastern Orthodox Church does not oppose honest critical and historical study of the Bible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ware1991_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ware1991-213">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_expansion_and_doctrinal_integrity">Territorial expansion and doctrinal integrity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Territorial expansion and doctrinal integrity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As the church increased in size through the centuries, the logistic dynamics of operating such large entities shifted: patriarchs, metropolitans, archimandrites, abbots and abbesses, all rose up to cover certain points of administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[207]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Liturgy">Liturgy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Liturgy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Rite" title="Byzantine Rite">Byzantine Rite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_worship" title="Eastern Orthodox worship">Eastern Orthodox worship</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Rite_Orthodoxy" title="Western Rite Orthodoxy">Western Rite Orthodoxy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2020" data-file-width="1576" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg/220px-Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg/330px-Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg/440px-Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meister_der_Sophien-Kathedrale_von_Ohrid_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">Fresco</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basil_the_Great" title="Basil the Great">Basil the Great</a>, in the church of <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Sophia,_Ohrid" title="Church of Saint Sophia, Ohrid">Saint Sophia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohrid" title="Ohrid">Ohrid</a>. The saint is shown <a href="/wiki/Consecration" title="Consecration">consecrating</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacred_Mysteries" title="Sacred Mysteries">Gifts</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Divine_Liturgy" title="Divine Liturgy">Divine Liturgy</a> which bears his name.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_calendar">Church calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Church calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
Lesser cycles also run in tandem with the annual ones. A weekly cycle of days prescribes a specific focus for each day in addition to others that may be observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[208]</a></sup><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Each day of the Weekly Cycle is dedicated to certain special memorials. Sunday is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">Christ's Resurrection</a>; Monday honors the holy bodiless powers (angels, archangels, etc.); Tuesday is dedicated to the prophets and especially the greatest of the prophets, <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Forerunner and Baptist of the Lord</a>; Wednesday is consecrated to the Cross and recalls Judas' betrayal; Thursday honors the holy apostles and hierarchs, especially <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">Nicholas, Bishop of Myra in Lycia</a>; Friday is also consecrated to the Cross and recalls the day of the Crucifixion; Saturday is dedicated to All Saints, especially the <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Mother of God</a>, and to the memory of all those who have departed this life in the hope of resurrection and eternal life.</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_services">Church services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Church services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canonical_hours#Byzantine_Rite_usage" title="Canonical hours">Canonical hours § Byzantine Rite usage</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b>  You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_chanting">Music and chanting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music and chanting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg/220px-Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg/330px-Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg/440px-Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patriarchate_Constantinopolis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chanters singing on the <a href="/wiki/Kliros" title="Kliros">kliros</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_St._George,_Istanbul" title="Church of St. George, Istanbul">Church of St. George</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Patriarchate of Constantinople">Patriarchate of Constantinople</a></div></div></div>
<p>The church has developed eight modes or tones (see <a href="/wiki/Octoechos" title="Octoechos">Octoechos</a>) within which a chant may be set, depending on the time of year, feast day, or other considerations of the <a href="/wiki/Typikon" title="Typikon">Typikon</a>. There are numerous versions and styles that are traditional and acceptable and these vary a great deal between cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993238_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993238-216">[209]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Art and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_church_architecture" title="Eastern Orthodox church architecture">Eastern Orthodox church architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg/240px-Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg/360px-Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg/480px-Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orthodox-Church-interior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An illustration of the traditional interior of an Orthodox church.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Archdiocesan_Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity" title="Archdiocesan Cathedral of the Holy Trinity">Archdiocesan Cathedral of the Holy Trinity</a> on New York City's <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">Upper East Side</a> is the largest Orthodox Christian church in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StudentEd_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-StudentEd-217">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_customs">Local customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Local customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg/180px-Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg/270px-Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg/360px-Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Broken_vases_on_Holy_Saturday_in_Corfu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shards of pottery vases on the street, after being thrown from the windows of nearby houses. A <a href="/wiki/Holy_Saturday" title="Holy Saturday">Holy Saturday</a> tradition in <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Locality is also expressed in regional terms of churchly jurisdiction, which is often also drawn along national lines. Many Orthodox churches adopt a national title (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Autocephalous_Church_of_Albania" title="Orthodox Autocephalous Church of Albania">Albanian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Orthodox</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiochian_Orthodox_Church" title="Antiochian Orthodox Church">Antiochian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Romanian Orthodox Church">Romanian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox" title="Ukrainian Orthodox">Ukrainian Orthodox</a>, etc.) and this title can identify which language is used in services, which bishops preside, and which of the typica is followed by specific <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/congregation" title="wikt:congregation">congregations</a>. In the Middle East, Orthodox Christians are usually referred to as <i>Rum</i> ("Roman") Orthodox, because of their historical connection with the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Eastern Roman (Byzantine) Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBinns20023_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBinns20023-218">[211]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Holy_mysteries_.28sacraments.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_mysteries_(sacraments)">Holy mysteries (sacraments)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Holy mysteries (sacraments)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Those things which in the West are often termed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacraments" title="Sacraments">sacraments</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacramentals" title="Sacramentals">sacramentals</a> are known among the Eastern Orthodox as the "sacred mysteries". While the Roman Catholic Church numbers seven sacraments, and many Protestant groups list two (baptism and the Eucharist) or even none, the Eastern Orthodox do not limit the number. However, for the sake of convenience, <a href="/wiki/Catechism" title="Catechism">catechisms</a> will often speak of the seven great mysteries. Among these are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Communion" title="Holy Communion">Holy Communion</a> (the most direct connection), <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chrismation" title="Chrismation">Chrismation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confession_(religion)" title="Confession (religion)">confession</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unction" title="Unction">unction</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrimony" title="Matrimony">matrimony</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ordination" title="Ordination">ordination</a>. But the term also properly applies to other sacred actions such as monastic <a href="/wiki/Tonsure" title="Tonsure">tonsure</a> or the blessing of <a href="/wiki/Holy_water_in_Eastern_Christianity" title="Holy water in Eastern Christianity">holy water</a>, and involves fasting, almsgiving, or an act as simple as lighting a candle, burning incense, praying or asking God's blessing on food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993274–277_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993274–277-219">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baptism">Baptism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Baptism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg/220px-GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg/330px-GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg/440px-GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GreekOrthodoxBaptism1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Eastern Orthodox baptism</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">Baptism</a> is the mystery which transforms the old and sinful person into a new and pure one; the old life, the sins, any mistakes made are gone and a clean slate is given. Through baptism a person is united to the <a href="/wiki/Body_of_Christ" title="Body of Christ">Body of Christ</a> by becoming a member of the Eastern Orthodox Church. During the service, <a href="/wiki/Holy_water_in_Eastern_Christianity" title="Holy water in Eastern Christianity">water</a> is blessed. The catechumen is fully immersed in the water three times in the name of the Trinity. This is considered to be a death of the "old man" by participation in the crucifixion and burial of Christ, and a rebirth into new life in Christ by participation in his resurrection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993277–278_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993277–278-220">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Properly, the mystery of baptism is administered by bishops and priests; however, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_baptism" title="Emergency baptism">in emergencies any Eastern Orthodox Christian can baptise</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993278_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993278-221">[214]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chrismation">Chrismation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Chrismation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chrismation" title="Chrismation">Chrismation</a> (sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Confirmation" title="Confirmation">confirmation</a>) is the mystery by which a baptised person is granted the gift of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">Holy Spirit</a> through anointing with Holy <a href="/wiki/Chrism" title="Chrism">Chrism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993278–279_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993278–279-223">[216]</a></sup> It is normally given immediately after baptism as part of the same service, but is also used to receive lapsed members of the Eastern Orthodox Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarakas198756–57_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarakas198756–57-224">[217]</a></sup> As baptism is a person's participation in the death and resurrection of Christ, so Chrismation is a person's participation in the coming of the Holy Spirit at <a href="/wiki/Pentecost" title="Pentecost">Pentecost</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ware1993p279_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-ware1993p279-225">[218]</a></sup>
</p><p>A baptised and chrismated Eastern Orthodox Christian is a full member of the church and may receive the Eucharist regardless of age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ware1993p279_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-ware1993p279-225">[218]</a></sup>
</p><p>The creation of Chrism may be accomplished by any bishop at any time, but usually is done only once a year, often when a synod of bishops convenes for its annual meeting. Some autocephalous churches get their chrism from others. Anointing with it substitutes for the laying-on of hands described in the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a>, even when an instrument such as a brush is used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarakas198757_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarakas198757-226">[219]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Holy_Communion_.28Eucharist.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_Communion_(Eucharist)">Holy Communion (Eucharist)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Holy Communion (Eucharist)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg/220px-Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg/330px-Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg/440px-Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liturgy_St_James_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eucharistic elements prepared for the Divine Liturgy</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Communion</a> is given only to baptised and chrismated Eastern Orthodox Christians who have prepared by fasting, prayer and confession. The priest will administer the gifts with a spoon, called a "cochlear", directly into the recipient's mouth from the chalice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993287_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993287-227">[220]</a></sup> From baptism young infants and children are carried to the chalice to receive holy communion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ware1993p279_225-2"><a href="#cite_note-ware1993p279-225">[218]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Repentance_.28Confession.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Repentance_(Confession)">Repentance (Confession)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Repentance (Confession)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Confession_(religion)" title="Confession (religion)">Confession (religion)</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b>  You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marriage_in_the_Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Marriage in the Eastern Orthodox Church">Marriage in the Eastern Orthodox Church</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_(1895,_Hermitage).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1433" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg/250px-Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg/375px-Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg/500px-Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_%281895%2C_Hermitage%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wedding_of_Nicholas_II_and_Alexandra_Feodorovna_by_Laurits_Tuxen_(1895,_Hermitage).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The wedding of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II of Russia</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>From the Orthodox perspective, marriage is one of the holy mysteries or sacraments. As well as in many other Christian traditions, for example in Catholicism, it serves to unite a woman and a man in eternal union and love before God, with the purpose of following Christ and his Gospel and raising up a faithful, holy family through their holy union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[222]</a></sup> The church understands marriage to be the union of one man and one woman, and certain Orthodox leaders have spoken out strongly in opposition to the civil institution of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jesus said that "when they rise from the dead, they neither marry nor are given in marriage, but are like angels in heaven" (Mk 12:25). For the Orthodox Christian this passage should not be understood to imply that Christian marriage will not remain a reality in the Kingdom, but points to the fact that relations will not be "fleshy", but "spiritual".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meyendorff70_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-meyendorff70-232">[225]</a></sup> Love between wife and husband, as an icon of relationship between Christ and church, is eternal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meyendorff70_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-meyendorff70-232">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>The church does recognise that there are rare occasions when it is better that couples do separate, but there is no official recognition of civil divorces. For the Eastern Orthodox, to say that marriage is indissoluble means that it should not be broken, the violation of such a union, perceived as holy, being an offense resulting from either adultery or the prolonged absence of one of the partners. Thus, permitting remarriage is an act of compassion of the church towards sinful man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holy_orders">Holy orders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Holy orders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kheirotonia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2024" data-file-width="2872" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kheirotonia.jpg/250px-Kheirotonia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kheirotonia.jpg/375px-Kheirotonia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kheirotonia.jpg/500px-Kheirotonia.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kheirotonia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eastern Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Subdeacon" title="Subdeacon">subdeacon</a> being ordained to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diaconate" title="Diaconate">diaconate</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">bishop</a> has placed his <a href="/wiki/Omophorion" title="Omophorion">omophorion</a> and right hand on the head of the candidate and is reading the <i>Prayer of <a href="/wiki/Christian_laying_on_of_hands" title="Christian laying on of hands">Cheirotonia</a></i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Widowed priests and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deacons" title="Deacons">deacons</a> may not remarry and it is common for such members of the clergy to retire to a monastery (see <a href="/wiki/Clerical_celibacy" title="Clerical celibacy">clerical celibacy</a>). This is also true of widowed wives of clergy, who do not remarry and become nuns when their children are grown. Only men are allowed to receive <a href="/wiki/Holy_orders" title="Holy orders">holy orders</a>, although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deaconesses" title="Deaconesses">deaconesses</a> had both liturgical and pastoral functions within the church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karras_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karras-234">[227]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the Patriarchate of Alexandria decided to reintroduce the order of deaconess.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[229]</a></sup> In February 2017, <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Theodore_II_of_Alexandria" title="Patriarch Theodore II of Alexandria">Patriarch Theodoros II</a> consecrated five women to be deaconesses within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Greek Orthodox Church of Alexandria">Patriarchate of Alexandria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[230]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unction">Unction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Unction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unction" title="Unction">Unction</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Empty_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section is empty.</b>  You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2021</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interfaith_relations">Interfaith relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Interfaith relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1128" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg/220px-Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg/330px-Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg/440px-Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fond-du-lac-circus.preview.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The consecration of <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Heber_Weller" title="Reginald Heber Weller">Reginald Heber Weller</a> as an Anglican bishop at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Cathedral,_Fond_du_Lac" title="St. Paul's Cathedral, Fond du Lac">Cathedral of St. Paul the Apostle</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Fond_du_Lac" title="Episcopal Diocese of Fond du Lac">Episcopal Diocese of Fond du Lac</a>, with Anthony Kozlowski of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_National_Catholic_Church" title="Polish National Catholic Church">Polish National Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Tikhon_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch Tikhon of Moscow">Tikhon, then Bishop of the Aleutians and Alaska</a> (along with his chaplains <a href="/wiki/John_Kochurov" title="John Kochurov">John Kochurov</a> and Sebastian Dabovich) of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> present</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_(1).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/220px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/330px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/440px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_I_of_Constantinople" title="Bartholomew I of Constantinople">Patriarch Bartholomew I</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">Church of the Holy Sepulchre</a>, Jerusalem, 2014</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_other_Christians">Relations with other Christians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Relations with other Christians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1920, the Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople, published an encyclical "addressed 'To all the Churches of Christ, wherever they may be', urging closer co-operation among separated Christians, and suggesting a 'League of Churches', parallel to the newly founded <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ware1993_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ware1993-238">[231]</a></sup> This gesture was instrumental in the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/World_Council_of_Churches" title="World Council of Churches">World Council of Churches</a> (WCC);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fuchs2008_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fuchs2008-239">[232]</a></sup> as such, almost all Eastern Orthodox churches are members of the WCC and "Orthodox ecclesiastics and theologians serve on its committees".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benz2008_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Benz2008-240">[233]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kallistos_Ware" title="Kallistos Ware">Kallistos Ware</a>, a British metropolitan bishop of the Orthodox Church, has stated that <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">ecumenism</a> "is important for Orthodoxy: it has helped to force the various Orthodox churches out of their comparative isolation, making them meet one another and enter into a living contact with non-Orthodox Christians."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWare1993322_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWare1993322-241">[234]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilarion_Alfeyev" title="Hilarion Alfeyev">Hilarion Alfeyev</a>, Metropolitan of Volokolamsk and head of external relations for the Moscow Patriarchate of the Russian Orthodox Church, stated that Orthodox and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestant</a> Christians share the same positions on "such issues as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">abortion</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Family_values#Conservative_definitions" title="Family values">family</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_marriage" title="Christian views on marriage">marriage</a>" and desire "vigorous grassroots engagement" between the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communion_(Christian)" title="Communion (Christian)">Christian communions</a> on such issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Communions_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Communions-242">[235]</a></sup>
In that regard, the differences between the Catholic and Eastern Orthodox communions have not been improved in any relevant way. Dogmatic and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liturgical" title="Liturgical">liturgical</a> polarities have been significant, even and especially in recent times. A pertinent point of contention between the monarchically papal, administratively centralised Catholic Church and the decentralised confederation of Orthodox churches is the theological significance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[236]</a></sup> During his visit to <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> in October 2016, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> was snubbed by most Orthodox Christians as he led mass before a practically empty <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Meskhi_Stadium" title="Mikheil Meskhi Stadium">Mikheil Meskhi Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[237]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Oriental Orthodox Churches are not in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communion_(Christian)" title="Communion (Christian)">communion</a> with the Eastern Orthodox Church, despite their similar names. Slow dialogue towards restoring communion between the two churches began in the mid-20th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Common_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Common-245">[238]</a></sup> and, notably, in the 19th century, when the Greek Patriarch in Egypt had to absent himself from the country for a long period of time; he left his church under the guidance of the Coptic <a href="/wiki/Pope_Cyril_IV_of_Alexandria" title="Pope Cyril IV of Alexandria">Pope Cyril IV of Alexandria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[239]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, the Primate of the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">OCU</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_of_Kyiv_and_all_Ukraine" title="Metropolitan of Kyiv and all Ukraine">Metropolitan of Kyiv and All Ukraine</a> <a href="/wiki/Epiphanius_I_of_Ukraine" title="Epiphanius I of Ukraine">Epiphanius</a> stated that "theoretically" the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Ukrainian Greek Catholic Church">Ukrainian Greek Catholic Church</a> could in the future unite into a united church around the Kyiv throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[240]</a></sup> In 2019, the Primate of the UGCC, <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_leaders_of_the_Ukrainian_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Lists of leaders of the Ukrainian Greek Catholic Church">Major Archbishop of Kyiv-Galicia</a> <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_Shevchuk" title="Sviatoslav Shevchuk">Sviatoslav</a>, stated that every effort should be made to restore the original unity of the Kyivan Church in its Orthodox and Catholic branches, saying that the restoration of Eucharistic communion between <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Rome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Constantinople</a> is not a utopia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>Notwithstanding certain overtures by both Roman Catholic and Eastern Orthodox leaders, the majority of Orthodox Christians, as well as Catholics, are not in favor of communion between their churches, with only a median of 35 percent and 38 percent, respectively, claiming support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-129">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_Islam">Relations with Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Relations with Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="908" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg/220px-1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg/330px-1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg/440px-1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1821_atrocities_Constantinople.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constantinople_Massacre_of_1821" title="Constantinople Massacre of 1821">Constantinople Massacre of April 1821</a>: a religious persecution of the Greek population of <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> under the Ottomans. Patriarch <a href="/wiki/Gregory_V_of_Constantinople" title="Gregory V of Constantinople">Gregory V of Constantinople</a> was executed.</div></div></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Bat_Ye%27or" title="Bat Ye'or">Bat Ye'or</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhimma" title="Dhimma">Christians under Islamic rule</a> were <a href="/wiki/Rum_Millet" title="Rum Millet">denied equality of rights</a> since they were forced to pay the <i><a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">jizya</a></i> poll tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Metropolitan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilarion_Alfeyev" title="Hilarion Alfeyev">Alfeyev</a> expressed the possibility of peaceful coexistence between Islam and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> in Russia, as the two religions have never had religious wars in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alfeyev_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alfeyev-250">[243]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Constituencies">Constituencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Constituencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_organization" title="Eastern Orthodox Church organization">List of the current autocephalous Eastern Orthodox churches and their dependencies</a></div>
<p>The various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocephalous" title="Autocephalous">autocephalous</a> and autonomous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synods" title="Synods">synods</a> of the Eastern Orthodox Church are distinct in terms of administration and local culture, but for the most part exist in <a href="/wiki/Full_communion" title="Full communion">full communion</a> with one another. In addition, some schismatic churches not in any communion exist, with all three groups identifying as Eastern Orthodox.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%CE%A0%CE%B1%CF%81%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CF%84%CE%BF%CF%85_%CE%A5%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%81%CE%B3%CE%BF%CF%8D_%CE%95%CE%BE%CF%89%CF%84%CE%B5%CF%81%CE%B9%CE%BA%CF%8E%CE%BD_%CE%9D._%CE%9A%CE%BF%CF%84%CE%B6%CE%B9%CE%AC_%CF%83%CF%84%CE%B7%CE%BD_%CE%91%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CE%BA%CE%B1%CE%B9_%CE%9C%CE%B5%CE%B3%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B7_%CE%A3%CF%8D%CE%BD%CE%BF%CE%B4%CE%BF_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%9F%CF%81%CE%B8%CF%8C%CE%B4%CE%BF%CE%BE%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%95%CE%BA%CE%BA%CE%BB%CE%B7%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1%CF%82,_%CE%9A%CF%81%CE%AE%CF%84%CE%B7,_16-27-6-2016_(27614224782).jpg"><img
