srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/%CE%A0%CE%B1%CF%81%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CF%84%CE%BF%CF%85_%CE%A5%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%81%CE%B3%CE%BF%CF%8D_%CE%95%CE%BE%CF%89%CF%84%CE%B5%CF%81%CE%B9%CE%BA%CF%8E%CE%BD_%CE%9D._%CE%9A%CE%BF%CF%84%CE%B6%CE%B9%CE%AC_%CF%83%CF%84%CE%B7%CE%BD_%CE%91%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CE%BA%CE%B1%CE%B9_%CE%9C%CE%B5%CE%B3%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B7_%CE%A3%CF%8D%CE%BD%CE%BF%CE%B4%CE%BF_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%9F%CF%81%CE%B8%CF%8C%CE%B4%CE%BF%CE%BE%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%95%CE%BA%CE%BA%CE%BB%CE%B7%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1%CF%82%2C_%CE%9A%CF%81%CE%AE%CF%84%CE%B7%2C_16-27-6-2016_%2827614224782%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/%CE%A0%CE%B1%CF%81%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CF%84%CE%BF%CF%85_%CE%A5%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%81%CE%B3%CE%BF%CF%8D_%CE%95%CE%BE%CF%89%CF%84%CE%B5%CF%81%CE%B9%CE%BA%CF%8E%CE%BD_%CE%9D._%CE%9A%CE%BF%CF%84%CE%B6%CE%B9%CE%AC_%CF%83%CF%84%CE%B7%CE%BD_%CE%91%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CE%BA%CE%B1%CE%B9_%CE%9C%CE%B5%CE%B3%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B7_%CE%A3%CF%8D%CE%BD%CE%BF%CE%B4%CE%BF_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%9F%CF%81%CE%B8%CF%8C%CE%B4%CE%BF%CE%BE%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%95%CE%BA%CE%BA%CE%BB%CE%B7%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1%CF%82%2C_%CE%9A%CF%81%CE%AE%CF%84%CE%B7%2C_16-27-6-2016_%2827614224782%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%CE%A0%CE%B1%CF%81%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CF%84%CE%BF%CF%85_%CE%A5%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%85%CF%81%CE%B3%CE%BF%CF%8D_%CE%95%CE%BE%CF%89%CF%84%CE%B5%CF%81%CE%B9%CE%BA%CF%8E%CE%BD_%CE%9D._%CE%9A%CE%BF%CF%84%CE%B6%CE%B9%CE%AC_%CF%83%CF%84%CE%B7%CE%BD_%CE%91%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1_%CE%BA%CE%B1%CE%B9_%CE%9C%CE%B5%CE%B3%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B7_%CE%A3%CF%8D%CE%BD%CE%BF%CE%B4%CE%BF_%CF%84%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%9F%CF%81%CE%B8%CF%8C%CE%B4%CE%BF%CE%BE%CE%B7%CF%82_%CE%95%CE%BA%CE%BA%CE%BB%CE%B7%CF%83%CE%AF%CE%B1%CF%82,_%CE%9A%CF%81%CE%AE%CF%84%CE%B7,_16-27-6-2016_(27614224782).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pan-Orthodox_Council" title="Pan-Orthodox Council">Pan-Orthodox Council</a>, Kolymvari, Crete, Greece, June 2016</div></div></div>
<p>Another group of non-mainstream Eastern Orthodox Christians are referred <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Orthodoxy" title="True Orthodoxy">True Orthodoxy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Old_Calendarists" title="Old Calendarists">Old Calendarists</a>; they are those who, without authority from their parent churches, have continued to use the old <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>, and split from their parent church.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church_Outside_Russia" title="Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia">Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia</a> (ROCOR) has <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Canonical_Communion_with_the_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Act of Canonical Communion with the Moscow Patriarchate">united in 2007 with the Moscow Patriarchate</a>; these two churches had separated from each other in the 1920s due to the subjection of the latter to the hostile <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet regime</a>.
</p><p>Another group called the <a href="/wiki/Old_Believers" title="Old Believers">Old Believers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raskol" title="Raskol">separated in 1666</a> from the official Russian Orthodox Church as a protest against church rite reforms introduced by <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Nikon_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch Nikon of Moscow">Patriarch Nikon of Moscow</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_communion">Main communion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Main communion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="533" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg/220px-AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg/330px-AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg/440px-AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlexGreekCathedralFront.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Evangelismos" title="Cathedral of Evangelismos">Cathedral of Evangelismos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Eastern Orthodox Church is a <a href="/wiki/Full_communion" title="Full communion">communion</a> of 15 <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephalous</a>—that is, administratively completely independent—regional churches,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[244]</a></sup> plus the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_America" title="Orthodox Church in America">Orthodox Church in America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a>. The Orthodox Church in America is recognised as autocephalous only by the Russian, Bulgarian, Georgian, Polish and Czech-Slovak churches. In December 2018, representatives of two unrecognized Ukrainian Orthodox churches, along with two <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitans</a> of the recognized, but not autocephalous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_of_the_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church of the Moscow Patriarchate">Ukrainian Orthodox Church of the Moscow Patriarchate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unification_council_of_the_Eastern_Orthodox_churches_of_Ukraine" title="Unification council of the Eastern Orthodox churches of Ukraine">proclaimed the formation of the unified Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a>. On 5 January 2019, the Orthodox Church of Ukraine received its <i><a href="/wiki/Tomos_(Eastern_Orthodox_Church)" title="Tomos (Eastern Orthodox Church)">tomos</a></i> of autocephaly (decree which defines the conditions of a church's independence) from the Ecumenical Patriarchate and thus received a place in the <a href="/wiki/Diptych#Ecclesiastical" title="Diptych">diptych</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/220px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/330px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg/440px-Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patrikana_e_Pej%C3%ABs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Pe%C4%87_(monastery)" title="Patriarchate of Peć (monastery)">Patriarchate of Peć</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> from the 14th century when its status was upgraded into a patriarchate</div></div></div>
<p>Each church has defined geographical boundaries of its jurisdiction and is ruled by its council of bishops or synod presided by a senior bishop–its <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">primate</a> (or first hierarch). The primate may carry the honorary title of patriarch, metropolitan (in the Slavic tradition) or archbishop (in the Greek tradition).
</p><p>Each regional church consists of constituent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eparchies" title="Eparchies">eparchies</a> (or dioceses) ruled by a bishop. Some churches have given an eparchy or group of eparchies varying degrees of <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_(Eastern_Orthodoxy)" title="Autonomy (Eastern Orthodoxy)">autonomy</a> (self-government). Such autonomous churches maintain varying levels of dependence on their <a href="/wiki/Mother_church" title="Mother church">mother church</a>, usually defined in a <a href="/wiki/Tomos_(Eastern_Orthodox_Church)" title="Tomos (Eastern Orthodox Church)"><i>tomos</i></a> or other document of autonomy.
</p><p>Below is a list of the 14 autocephalous Orthodox churches forming the main body of Orthodox Christianity, all of which are titled equal to each other, but the Ecumenical Patriarchate is titled the <i>first among equals</i>. Based on the definitions, the list is in the order of precedence and alphabetical order where necessary, with some of their constituent autonomous churches and exarchates listed as well. The liturgical title of the primate is in italics.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople</a> (<i>Archbishop of Constantinople-New Rome and First Among Equals Patriarch</i>)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Archdiocese_of_Italy" title="Orthodox Archdiocese of Italy">Orthodox Archdiocese of Italy</a> (<i>Orthodox Archbishop of Italy</i>)</li>
<li>Autonomous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finnish_Orthodox_Church" title="Finnish Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Finland</a> (<i>Archbishop of Helsinki and All Finland</i>, formerly <i>Archbishop of Karelia and All Finland</i>)</li>
<li>Self-governing Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Crete" title="Church of Crete">Church of Crete</a> (<i>Archbishop of Crete</i>)</li>
<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Monastic_community_of_Mount_Athos" title="Monastic community of Mount Athos">monastic community of Mount Athos</a></li>
<li>Self-governing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_Orthodox_Church" title="Korean Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Korea</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Seoul and All Korea</i>)</li>
<li>Exarchate of Malta</li>
<li>Eparchy of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_of_Canada" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church of Canada">Ukrainian Orthodox Church of Canada</a></li>
<li>Eparchy of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_of_the_USA" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church of the USA">Ukrainian Orthodox Church of the USA</a></li>
<li>Eparchy of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Archdiocese_of_America" title="Greek Orthodox Archdiocese of America">Greek Orthodox Archdiocese of America</a></li>
<li>Eparchy of the <a href="/wiki/Exarchate_of_the_Philippines" title="Exarchate of the Philippines">Exarchate of the Philippines</a></li>
<li>Eparchy of the <a href="/wiki/American_Carpatho-Russian_Orthodox_Diocese" title="American Carpatho-Russian Orthodox Diocese">American Carpatho-Russian Orthodox Diocese</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Alexandria" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Alexandria">Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Alexandria</a> (<i>the Pope and Patriarch of the Great City of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentapolis_(North_Africa)" title="Pentapolis (North Africa)">Pentapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, all the land of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and all Africa</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Antioch" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Antioch">Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Antioch</a> (<i>Patriarch of Antioch and all the East</i>)
<ul><li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Antiochian_Orthodox_Christian_Archdiocese_of_North_America" title="Antiochian Orthodox Christian Archdiocese of North America">Antiochian Orthodox Christian Archdiocese of North America</a> (<i>Archbishop of New York and Metropolitan of All North America</i>)</li>
<li>Self-governing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiochian_Orthodox_Archdiocese_of_Australia,_New_Zealand,_and_All_Oceania" title="Antiochian Orthodox Archdiocese of Australia, New Zealand, and All Oceania">Antiochian Orthodox Archdiocese of Australia, New Zealand, and All Oceania</a> (<i>Metropolitan Archbishop of Australia, New Zealand and the Philippines</i>)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Jerusalem" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Jerusalem">Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Jerusalem</a> (<i>Patriarch of the Holy City of Jerusalem and all Holy Land, Syria, Arabia, beyond the Jordan River, Cana of Galilee, and Sacred Zion</i>)
<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Sinai" title="Church of Sinai">Church of Mount Sinai</a> (<i>Archbishop of Choreb, Sinai, and Raitha</i>)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Patriarch of Moscow and all Russia</i>)
<ul><li>Autonomous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Orthodox_Church" title="Japanese Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church in Japan</a> (<i>Archbishop of Tokyo and Metropolitan of All Japan</i>)</li>
<li>Exarchate of <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Orthodox Church">Belarus</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Minsk and Slutsk, Patriarchal Exarch of All Belarus</i>)</li>
<li>Self-governing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church_Outside_Russia" title="Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia">Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Eastern America and New York, First Hierarch of the Russian church abroad</i>)</li>
<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Orthodox_Church" title="Latvian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Latvia</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Riga and all Latvia</i>)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Archbishop of Peć, Metropolitan of Belgrade and Karlovci, and Serbian Patriarch</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Sofia and Patriarch of All Bulgaria</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Romanian Orthodox Church">Romanian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Archbishop of Bucharest, Metropolitan of Muntenia and Dobrudja, Locum Tenens of the Throne of Caesarea of Cappadocia, and Patriarch of Romania</i>)
<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Metropolis_of_the_Americas" title="Romanian Orthodox Metropolis of the Americas">Romanian Orthodox Metropolis of the Americas</a> (<i>Romanian Orthodox Archbishop of the United States of America and Romanian Orthodox Metropolitan of the Americas</i>)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Catholicos-Patriarch of All Georgia, the Archbishop of Mtskheta-Tbilisi and Metropolitan bishop of Abkhazia and Pitsunda</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Cyprus" title="Church of Cyprus">Church of Cyprus</a> (<i>Archbishop of New Justiniana and all Cyprus</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Greece" title="Church of Greece">Church of Greece</a> (<i>Archbishop of Athens and all Greece</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Albanian Orthodox Church">Albanian Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Archbishop of Tirana, Durres and all Albania</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Polish_Orthodox_Church" title="Polish Orthodox Church">Polish Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Warsaw and all Poland</i> or <i>Archbishop of Warsaw and Metropolitan of All Poland)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[h]</a></sup></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_the_Czech_Lands_and_Slovakia" title="Orthodox Church of the Czech Lands and Slovakia">Orthodox Church of the Czech Lands and Slovakia</a> (<i>Archbishop of Prague, the Metropolitan of Czech lands and Slovakia or the Archbishop of Presov, the Metropolitan of Czech lands and Slovakia</i>)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church_%E2%80%93_Ohrid_Archbishopric" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church – Ohrid Archbishopric">Macedonian Orthodox Church – Ohrid Archbishopric</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Skopje and Archbishop of Ohrid and Macedonia and of Justiniana Prima</i>)</li></ul>
</div>
<p>Within the main body of Eastern Orthodoxy there are unresolved internal issues as to the autonomous or autocephalous status or legitimacy of the following Orthodox churches, particularly between those stemming from the Russian Orthodox or Constantinopolitan churches:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="div-col">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_America" title="Orthodox Church in America">Orthodox Church in America</a> (<i>Archbishop of Washington, Metropolitan of All America and Canada</i>) – Not recognised by the Ecumenical Patriarchate.</li>
<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Apostolic_Orthodox_Church" title="Estonian Apostolic Orthodox Church">Estonian Apostolic Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Tallinn and all Estonia</i>) – Recognised only by the Ecumenical Patriarchate, opposed only by the Russian Orthodox Church.</li>
<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Orthodox_Church_of_the_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Estonian Orthodox Church of the Moscow Patriarchate">Estonian Orthodox Church of the Moscow Patriarchate</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Tallinn and all Estonia</i>) – Not recognised by the Ecumenical Patriarchate.</li>
<li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Bessarabia" title="Metropolis of Bessarabia">Bessarabian Orthodox Church</a> in Moldova (<i>Archbishop of Chișinău, Metropolitan of Bessarabia and Exarch of the Territories</i>) of the Romanian Orthodox Church – Territory claimed by the Russian Orthodox Church.</li>
<li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_and_All_Moldova" title="Metropolis of Chișinău and All Moldova">Moldovan Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Chișinău and all Moldova</i>) of the Russian Orthodox Church – Jurisdiction disputed by the Romanian Orthodox Church.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Ukraine" title="Orthodox Church of Ukraine">Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Kyiv and All Ukraine</i>) – Recognised by the Ecumenical Patriarchate, Church of Greece, Church of Cyprus, and Patriarchate of Alexandria<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BS1_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-BS1-254">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BS2_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-BS2-256">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BS3_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-BS3-257">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[251]</a></sup> as of October 2020, opposed by the Russian, Antiochian, Czech and Slovak, Serbian and Polish Orthodox Churches, and the Orthodox Church in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[254]</a></sup></li></ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditionalist_groups">Traditionalist groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Traditionalist groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="True_Orthodox">True Orthodox</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: True Orthodox">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_organization#True_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox Church organization">Eastern Orthodox Church organization § True Orthodox</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Orthodoxy" title="True Orthodoxy">True Orthodoxy</a> has been separated from the mainstream communion over issues of ecumenism and calendar reform since the 1920s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politika2_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-politika2-263">[255]</a></sup> The movement rejects the Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople, the Moscow Patriarchate, and all churches which are in communion with them, accusing them of heresy and placing themselves under bishops who do the same thing. They adhere to the use of the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>, claiming that the <a href="/wiki/Revised_Julian_calendar" title="Revised Julian calendar">calendar reform in the 1920s</a> is in contradiction with the ecumenical councils. There is no official communion of True Orthodox; and they often are local groups and are limited to a specific bishop or locality.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_calendarists">Old calendarists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Old calendarists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Old_Calendarists" title="Old Calendarists">Old Calendarists</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Believers">Old Believers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Old Believers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Old_Believers#Old_Believer_churches" title="Old Believers">Old Believers § Old Believer churches</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/220px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/330px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/440px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Paschal</a> procession by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Old-Rite_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Old-Rite Church">Russian Orthodox Old-Rite Church</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Old_Believers" title="Old Believers">Old Believers</a> are groups which do not accept the liturgical reforms which were carried out within the Russian Orthodox Church by <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Nikon_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch Nikon of Moscow">Patriarch Nikon of Moscow</a> in the 17th century. Although all of the groups of Old Believers emerged as a result of opposition to the Nikonian reforms, they do not constitute a single monolithic body. Despite their emphasis on invariable adherence to the pre-Nikonian traditions, the Old Believers feature a great diversity of groups which profess different interpretations of church tradition and they are often not in communion with each other (some groups even practise re-baptism before admitting a member of another group into their midst).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches_not_in_communion_with_other_churches">Churches not in communion with other churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Churches not in communion with other churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church_organization#Churches_that_are_not_recognized_despite_wanting_to" title="Eastern Orthodox Church organization">Eastern Orthodox Church organization § Churches that are not recognized despite wanting to</a></div>
<p>Churches with irregular or unresolved canonical status are entities that have carried out <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Episcopi_vagantes" title="Episcopi vagantes">episcopal consecrations outside of the norms of canon law</a> or whose bishops have been excommunicated by one of the 14 autocephalous churches. These include nationalist and other schismatic bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_Orthodox_Church" title="Abkhazian Orthodox Church">Abkhazian Orthodox Church</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, as a whole, is not formally a church</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-149">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The numerous <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> groups in the world, if taken all together, substantially outnumber the Eastern Orthodox, but they differ theologically and do not form a single communion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiamondPlattnerCostopoulos2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidCTqTeiBfdxEClpgPP1pgPP1vonepageqffalse_119]_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiamondPlattnerCostopoulos2005[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidCTqTeiBfdxEClpgPP1pgPP1vonepageqffalse_119]-148">[147]</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Roman Lunkin in an interview about the 2012 survey published by <span title="Russian-language text"><span lang="ru">Среда</span></span> (<i><span title="Russian-language romanization"><i lang="ru-Latn">Sreda</i></span></i>), about 40% of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> population is Orthodox. However, only 5% belong to a parish or regularly attend Divine Liturgy. Lunkin said that this was long known by experts but a myth persists that 80–90% of the population is Orthodox.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> According to <i>The World Factbook</i> 2006 estimate, 15–20% are practicing Russian Orthodox but there is a large populations of non-practicing believers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAWeb_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWeb-156">[154]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-160"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-160">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Data are estimated, there are no census figures available, Greece is said to be 98% Orthodox by CIA, but additional studies found only 60–80% believe in God, if true, then no more than 80% may be Orthodox.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-161">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">With an absolute majority in the subnational entity of Republika Srpska</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-173"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-173">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Alexei Krindatch, "the total number of Orthodox parishes" increased by 16% from 2000 to 2010 in the United States, from this, he wrote that Orthodox Churches are growing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krindatch2010_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krindatch2010-172">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 2">: 2 </span></sup> Krindatch did not provide figures about any change in the membership over that same period in his 2010 highlight.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-176"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-176">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Oliver Herbel, in <i>Turning to Tradition</i>, the 2008 US Religious Landscape Survey "suggests that if there is growth, it is statistically insignificant."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herbel2014_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herbel2014-174">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 9">: 9 </span></sup> The 2014 US Religious Landscape Survey also shows, within the survey's ±9.2% margin of sampling error corresponding to the sample size of the <i>Orthodox Christian</i> category being 186 people, a statistically insignificant decline within the category "Orthodox Christians" as the percentage of population from 2007 to 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-175">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 4, 21, 36, 93">: 4, 21, 36, 93 </span></sup> But only 53% of people who were Orthodox Christian as children still self identify as Orthodox Christian in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-175">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 39">: 39 </span></sup> The <i>Orthodox Christian</i> category "is most heavily made up of immigrants and the children of immigrants."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-175">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 53">: 53 </span></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-253"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-253">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The primate of the Polish Orthodox Church is referred to as <i>Archbishop of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> and Metropolitan of All Poland</i>, but the Polish Orthodox Church is officially a Metropolis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[245]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

(2017-09-01) [1999]. "Western rite Orthodoxy". <a class="external text" href="http://doi.wiley.com/10.1002/9781405166584" rel="nofollow"><i>The Blackwell Dictionary of Eastern Christianity</i></a>. Oxford, UK: Blackwell Publishing Ltd. pp. 514–5. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1002%2F9781405166584" rel="nofollow">10.1002/9781405166584</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4051-6658-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4051-6658-4"><bdi>978-1-4051-6658-4</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Western+rite+Orthodoxy&amp;rft.btitle=The+Blackwell+Dictionary+of+Eastern+Christianity&amp;rft.place=Oxford%2C+UK&amp;rft.pages=514-5&amp;rft.pub=Blackwell+Publishing+Ltd&amp;rft.date=2017-09-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1002%2F9781405166584&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4051-6658-4&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdoi.wiley.com%2F10.1002%2F9781405166584&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span></span>

<li id='cite_note-FOOTNOTECleenewerck2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidoeKOUb6OcG4CpgPA101Holy_100–101]._The_word_"Catholic"_shows_that_the_church_consider_itself_[[Catholicity|universal_and_complete]],_and_not_to_be_confused_with_Catholicism._"The_Church_of_the_East_has_never_from_the_first_been_known_by_any_other_name_than_Catholic,_nor_has_she_set_aside_this_title_in_any_official_document."-31'><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href='#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECleenewerck2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidoeKOUb6OcG4CpgPA101Holy_100–101]._The_word_"Catholic"_shows_that_the_church_consider_itself_[[Catholicity|universal_and_complete]],_and_not_to_be_confused_with_Catholicism._"The_Church_of_the_East_has_never_from_the_first_been_known_by_any_other_name_than_Catholic,_nor_has_she_set_aside_this_title_in_any_official_document."_31-0'>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCleenewerck2009">Cleenewerck 2009</a>, pp. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=oeKOUb6OcG4C&amp;pg=PA101Holy" rel="nofollow">100–101</a>. The word "Catholic" shows that the church consider itself <a href="/wiki/Catholicity" title="Catholicity">universal and complete</a>, and not to be confused with Catholicism. "The Church of the East has never from the first been known by any other name than Catholic, nor has she set aside this title in any official document.".</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/topic/Eastern-Orthodoxy" rel="nofollow">"Eastern Orthodoxy | Definition, Origin, History, &amp; Facts | Britannica"</a>. <i>www.britannica.com</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-11-11</span></span>. <q>The official designation of the church in Eastern Orthodox liturgical or canonical texts is 'the Orthodox Catholic Church.' Because of the historical links of Eastern Orthodoxy with the Eastern Roman Empire and Byzantium (Constantinople), however, in English usage it is referred to as the 'Eastern' or 'Greek Orthodox' Church.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=www.britannica.com&amp;rft.atitle=Eastern+Orthodoxy+%7C+Definition%2C+Origin%2C+History%2C+%26+Facts+%7C+Britannica&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.britannica.com%2Ftopic%2FEastern-Orthodoxy&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica_Online[httpswwwbritannicacomEBcheckedtopic177174Eastern-Orthodoxy_&quot;Eastern_Orthodoxy&quot;]_&quot;Because_of_the_use_of_the_name_'Greek_Catholics'_by_the_Eastern_churches_of_the_Catholic_Church_and_the_historical_links_of_the_Orthodox_Catholic_church_with_the_Eastern_Roman_Empire_and_Byzantium_(Constantinople),_however,_the_[[exonym]]s_in_American_English_usage_referred_to_it_as_the_'Eastern'_or_'Greek_Orthodox'_Church._These_terms_are_sometimes_misleading,_especially_when_applied_to_Russian_or_Slavic_churches_and_to_the_Orthodox_communities_in_western_Europe_and_America.&quot;-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopædia_Britannica_Online[httpswwwbritannicacomEBcheckedtopic177174Eastern-Orthodoxy_&quot;Eastern_Orthodoxy&quot;]_&quot;Because_of_the_use_of_the_name_'Greek_Catholics'_by_the_Eastern_churches_of_the_Catholic_Church_and_the_historical_links_of_the_Orthodox_Catholic_church_with_the_Eastern_Roman_Empire_and_Byzantium_(Constantinople),_however,_the_[[exonym]]s_in_American_English_usage_referred_to_it_as_the_'Eastern'_or_'Greek_Orthodox'_Church._These_terms_are_sometimes_misleading,_especially_when_applied_to_Russian_or_Slavic_churches_and_to_the_Orthodox_communities_in_western_Europe_and_America.&quot;_51-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFEncyclopædia_Britannica_Online">Encyclopædia Britannica Online</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/177174/Eastern-Orthodoxy" rel="nofollow">"Eastern Orthodoxy"</a> "Because of the use of the name 'Greek Catholics' by the Eastern churches of the Catholic Church and the historical links of the Orthodox Catholic church with the Eastern Roman Empire and Byzantium (Constantinople), however, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exonym" title="Exonym">exonyms</a> in American English usage referred to it as the 'Eastern' or 'Greek Orthodox' Church. These terms are sometimes misleading, especially when applied to Russian or Slavic churches and to the Orthodox communities in western Europe and America.".</span>

<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFLogan1964">Logan, John B. (March 1964). "The Orthodox Church. By Timothy Ware. Penguin Books, Middlesex, 1963. Pp. 352. 6s". <i>Scottish Journal of Theology</i>. <b>17</b> (1): 117–119. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1017%2Fs0036930600006256" rel="nofollow">10.1017/s0036930600006256</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0036-9306" rel="nofollow">0036-9306</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Scottish+Journal+of+Theology&amp;rft.atitle=The+Orthodox+Church.+By+Timothy+Ware.+Penguin+Books%2C+Middlesex%2C+1963.+Pp.+352.+6s.&amp;rft.volume=17&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=117-119&amp;rft.date=1964-03&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2Fs0036930600006256&amp;rft.issn=0036-9306&amp;rft.aulast=Logan&amp;rft.aufirst=John+B.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-144">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2">"Gsell, Most Rev. Francis Xavier (27 Oct. 1872–12 July 1960), RC Bishop of Darwin, 1938–49; Titular Bishop of Paris; assistant at the Pontifical throne, Rome, 1951", <i>Who Was Who</i>, Oxford University Press, 2007-12-01, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1093%2Fww%2F9780199540884.013.u238027" rel="nofollow">10.1093/ww/9780199540884.013.u238027</a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Who+Was+Who&amp;rft.atitle=Gsell%2C+Most+Rev.+Francis+Xavier+%2827+Oct.+1872%E2%80%9312+July+1960%29%2C+RC+Bishop+of+Darwin%2C+1938%E2%80%9349%3B+Titular+Bishop+of+Paris%3B+assistant+at+the+Pontifical+throne%2C+Rome%2C+1951&amp;rft.date=2007-12-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1093%2Fww%2F9780199540884.013.u238027&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span>

"Everywhere following the decrees of the Holy Fathers, and aware of the recently recognized Canon of the one hundred and fifty most God-beloved Bishops who convened during the reign of Theodosius the Great of pious memory, who became emperor in the imperial city of Constantinople otherwise known as New Rome; we too decree and vote the same things in regard to the privileges and priorities of the most holy Church of that same Constantinople and New Rome. And this is in keeping with the fact that the Fathers naturally enough granted the priorities to the throne of Old Rome on account of her being the imperial capital. And motivated by the same object and aim the one hundred and fifty most God-beloved Bishops have accorded the like priorities to the most holy throne of New Rome, with good reason deeming that the city which is the seat of an empire, and of a senate, and is equal to old imperial Rome in respect of other privileges and priorities, should be magnified also as she is in respect of ecclesiastical affairs, as coming next after her, or as being second to her."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-145">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Christopher M. Bellitto, <i>The General Councils: A History of the Twenty-one General Councils from Nicaea to Vatican II</i>, Paulist Press, 2002, p. 41.</span>
</li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-11-12</span></span>. <q>Regarding the issue of the institution of Deaconesses, it was decided to revive this and a tripartite committee of Hierarchs was appointed for a detailed consideration of the subject.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=patriarchateofalexandria.com&amp;rft.atitle=Second+Day+of+Deliberations+of+the+Holy+Synod+of+the+Patriarchate+of+Alexandria&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.patriarchateofalexandria.com%2Findex.php%3Fmodule%3Dnews%26action%3Ddetails%26id%3D1207&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-237"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-237">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.ncronline.org/news/theology/orthodox-move-women-deacons-called-revitalization-not-innovation" rel="nofollow">"Orthodox move for women deacons is 'revitalization' not 'innovation'<span class="cs1-kern-right"></span>"</a>. <i>National Catholic Reporter</i>. 2017-11-30<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2021-11-12</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=National+Catholic+Reporter&amp;rft.atitle=Orthodox+move+for+women+deacons+is+%27revitalization%27+not+%27innovation%27&amp;rft.date=2017-11-30&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ncronline.org%2Fnews%2Ftheology%2Forthodox-move-women-deacons-called-revitalization-not-innovation&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Ware1993-238"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ware1993_238-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFWare1993">Ware 1993</a>, p. 322 "From the beginning of the twentieth century the Ecumenical Patriarchate has shown a special concern for Christian reconciliation. At his accession in 1902, Patriarch Joachim III sent an encyclical letter to all the autocephalous Orthodox Churches, asking in particular for their opinion on relations with other Christian bodies. In January 1920 the Ecumenical Patriarchate followed this up with a bold and prophetic letter addressed 'To all the Churches of Christ, wherever they may be', urging closer co-operation among separated Christians, and suggesting a 'League of Churches', parallel to the newly founded League of Nations. Many of the ideas in this letter anticipate subsequent developments in the WCC. Constantinople, along with several of the other Orthodox Churches, was represented at the Faith and Order Conferences at Lausanne in 1927 and at Edinburgh in 1937. The Ecumenical Patriarchate also participated in the first Assembly of the WCC at Amsterdam in 1948, and has been a consistent supporter of the work of the WCC ever since."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Fuchs2008-239"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Fuchs2008_239-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFuchs2008">Fuchs, Lorelei F. <li id="cite_note-note_n0-264"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-note_n0_264-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The ROC <a href="/wiki/2018_Moscow%E2%80%93Constantinople_schism" title="2018 Moscow–Constantinople schism">severed full communion</a> with the Ecumenical Patriarchate in 2018, and later severed full communion with the <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">primates</a> of the Church of Greece, the Patriarchate of Alexandria, and the Church of Cyprus in 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-note_n1-265"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n1_265-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Autocephaly or autonomy is not universally recognized.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-note_n3-266"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-note_n3_266-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">UOC-MP has moved to formally cut ties with the ROC as of May 27th 2022.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-note_n2-267"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-note_n2_267-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-note_n2_267-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Semi-autonomous part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> whose autonomy is not universally recognized.</span>
</li>
